    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_600416625" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/600416625" />
    <a title="Andre" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6431131-andre"><img alt="Andre" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1378118123p2/6431131.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/600416625?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andre" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andre" href="/user/show/6431131-andre">Andre</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6431131-andre?shelf=don-t-read-it">don-t-read-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6431131-andre?shelf=bisexual">bisexual</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6431131-andre?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer600416625" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6917291390297461922">Alternative title: <b>The bumbling around of a whiny, idiotic and judgmental asshole.</b><br/><br/>Note: There will be spoilers in this review and no possibility to blank them out, I think everyone reading this should know what they are in to when it comes to these stories.<br/><br/><br/>These stories (which I read when they were released as e-books) were utter crap!!!<br/>So far I read all of the Shadowhunter books apart from Clockwork Princess and City of Heavenly Fire and this here was the worst of them all in my mind. But to be</span>
  <span id="freeText6917291390297461922" style="display:none">Alternative title: <b>The bumbling around of a whiny, idiotic and judgmental asshole.</b><br /><br />Note: There will be spoilers in this review and no possibility to blank them out, I think everyone reading this should know what they are in to when it comes to these stories.<br /><br /><br />These stories (which I read when they were released as e-books) were utter crap!!!<br />So far I read all of the Shadowhunter books apart from Clockwork Princess and City of Heavenly Fire and this here was the worst of them all in my mind. But to be fair, this might simply be due to the fact that the stories here were shorter and so there was not so much other text to overshadow the inconsistencies, retcons, idiocy and plotholes. And there were many in this, trust me. One of the most easily explainable is Magnus' constant skin tone changes from gold to brown even when it contradicts the other books (you would have to come up with a pretty good explanation why in City of Bones he was golden and in the story here that plays less than a week later he is brown and in City of Ashes no one notices that change; plus I think when writing this the authors often had Godfrey Gao [who played him in the film adaptation of City of Bones] in mind and not the person introduced in TMI). There are more problems, like his age, relationships, power levels, but there is a character limit.<br /><br />The advertisement for this print at the time this review was written (29Sep2014) was telling us about its content:<br /><i>Ever wondered about the enigmatic, mysterious warlock Magnus Bane? The only character to appear in every Shadowhunter book, Magnus has a past even more shrouded in mystery than his present. I’ve teamed up with acclaimed YA writers Maureen Johnson and Sarah Rees Brennan to create the Bane Chronicles, the back (and front) story of Magnus told in ten linked tales.</i><br /><br />The stories are only very loosely linked and if these are anything to go by, Magnus's past isn't exactly <i>shrouded in mystery</i>, it's simply that in TMI he wouldn't even tell the boy he allegedly loved more than anyone else (not that I believed that, not with their lack of chemistry; these stories here didn't help with that either) the name he was given by his parents or even where he was born, his ex-girlfriend needed to do that and boy was she demonized by him here, not that her actions warranted that.<br />Now, in most of these 11 parts (the 1st and 9th have more than one story) we see Magnus interact with people we already know from the other books (what a waste of time) and in the one where there are none he does things that probably would have been known in history books (being a famous magician in late 18th century Parisean high society and even assisting Axel von Fersen in the royal family's botched flight). You can't write stuff like this (or have him be a wanted thief in several countries during the 1960s) and then act like his past is shrouded in mystery. Seriously, in TMI alone 4 people are mentioned, and three of them appear (Catarina Loss, Raphael Santiago and Camille Belcourt) who could have told you a lot about Magnus. The authors simply made it up here and didn't bother to check whether it fits.<br />And as for Magnus's back story: screw that! The earliest story has him being at least 84 years old and about his early years we in essence get told the same stuff we were told in The Mortal Instruments (TMI) and The Infernal Devices (TID) already, namely that his father was a demon, his mother killed herself over that (albeit when, I wonder, since what is presented here clashes with what was stated in TMI and TID) and his stepfather tried to kill him (also odd when this was supposed to be or why he kept the boy so long if he allegedly hated him so much).<br />Also his alleged diverse tastes are nowhere to be seen here, his lovers and people he generally fancies are predominantly male, young and white, mostly looking like Jace or Alec/Will. Also while we have him in relationships with women, the whole heads over falling for someone and describing their beauty is exclusively with guys. And only one of his lovers that we see might have not been white, but he was a Peruvian Mestizio so he might as well be white anyhow. Apart from that the books only refer to as "lovers," without any face, name, history or even appearing in the story. Their influence upon Magnus seems to be non-existent as well.<br /><br />There is very little of substance here and authors throw in serious topics without knowing what they are talking about and thereby screwing it all up. The Magnus we see here is a whiny asshole and an idiot, further evidence that these books truly have only one sort of main male protagonist since Jace of TMI and Will of TID were the same as well. Next to Magnus the Shadowhunters that he constantly whines about look downright reasonable, actually I think Magnus is the true racist asshole here and not them. Considered how he acts it's no wonder they don't like him, and the vampires here would give anyone ample reason to mistrust them. Magnus should have stopped judging other people and looked at his own vile attitude. Since that was also a problem here: Magnus doesn't want to be judged but he judges people all the time, even for their taste in clothes; even Alec he pitied just because Alec wasn't knowledgeable about some fashion designers.<br /><br />And oh gosh was Magnus, whiny, stupid and downright selfish and arrogant. I am sure this is not intentional, this might have been ok then, since the book constantly tries to create drama and make him look sympathetic and I think this is where the problem lies. The book only wants "drama and sympathy" no matter what. There is no caring about what makes sense, how it makes the characters look, there is no care about what is in-character when it doesn't fit the plot and especially no care about established characters and general canon. Even Magnus's age and experience is only there to serve for some half-assed explanations and to give him even more reason to whine. And to be honest, in the real world Magnus would have been dead meat a long time ago. But the forced plots would never allow for Magnus to even get a scratch.<br /><br />What these stories seem to lack is the passion for writing good characters and story, or having artwork fitting the stories. There is no hint that anyone ever took a step back and thought something like "What would this character do, how would this work, how could that work, how would these people act, what does this say about the character?" And I am not talking about the personality level; not even education or culture, albeit that is a huge problem was well. I am talking about more basic things: the abilities of the different species in this world, what they could do and how it would affect their behavior and thinking. There seems to have been no effort spent on the thought as to how a warlock with such power would act, what a vampire can do in this and that situation or how werewolves would go about things with the abilities they have. Nothing at all, it was either ignored or forgotten entirely as it seems and this is a huge part as to why this book is so stupid and annoying. And if it didn't have that problem, it would still not be good, because it would be boring. You see pretty much every major plot-point coming and if you care enough to think about it, the minor ones probably as well.<br /><br />I guess a lot of the stuff here is supposed to be funny but not only does the series repeat the same stuff over and over, but the "funny" stuff is totally misplaced (and keep in mind that this is not marketed under comedy) and lets Magnus look like an idiot without any sort of moral compass. And not just him.<br /><br />I think these stories are only enjoyable when you outright belief everything the text literally tells you without paying attention to what is actually presented and when you belief everything Magnus does is great no matter what.<br />I don't belong to these people and so reading this was painful and I needed several other books to act as an antidote.<br />Whenever Maureen Johnson was not involved the writing was awful and in general the stories are stupid and wow where they unnecessary.<br />As easy as it is to show what is wrong with this book, as easy would it be to do better for everybody reading this with just a little effort and an honest editor. But apparently these authors had neither.<br />The only good thing about this was that I started researching about Batavia and Victorian London and damn did the authors screw that up. No way is Magnus from 17th or 18th century Batavia.<br /><br />And just to make this clear:<br />I did not hate Magnus when I started with this. I never liked Magnus because of his major character flaws but I readily admit that he wasn't this asshole. I thought he was childish but I didn't hate him. I was curious as to what Clare would write and it was painful to get through this. These stories made me at first annoyed by Magnus, then I lost all respect for him and towards the end I hated him.<br />And mark that: <b>For me that was a first!!!</b><br />I never once before hated a fictional character as far as I can remember but Magnus Bane I hated when finishing this.<br /><br />Now let me tell you about these parts, in very short form of course, there is still a character limit. And its good there is since it's incredible how much the authors managed to do wrong in such a short amount of time and space.<br /><br /><u>
  <b>Part 1</b>
</u><br />These 4 stories were advertised to tell you why Magnus was banned from Peru. Forget that, in the end they do a cop-out and do the old "it shall remain a mystery" routine.<br />But that is not the biggest problem. That is the fact that when reading it I was constantly thinking "asshole" and "Jace" about Magnus. He was whiny, totally into himself, backstabbing, whimsical, shallow and sometimes close to bipolar if what he claims about himself and his emotions is true. Furthermore we have here what I consider a badly done clean-up job (since it never appeared anywhere else, ever) regarding the age inconsistencies for Magnus in TMI and TID: he lies about it out of habit (to everyone), making it vary widely.<br />Several times the thought "what did they smoke" crossed my mind. The characters don't really develop, a lot makes no sense or has no relevance, there is weird language and weird characters, with Magnus being the worst, and no real sense behind it all.<br />Full review: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/600644796">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a><br /><br /><u>
  <b>Part 2</b>
</u><br />This part happened, I think (they screwed up the time line), before the first story in part 1 (which opens some plotholes). This was slightly better than the first part but only in some ways. In the end Magnus just abandons the guy he previously would do everything for apparently just because he doesn't understand mundane politics. I am not kidding, that is the reason we are given and the thing is: Magnus was never involved in mundane politics, ever, so this comes right out of nowhere and makes the plot even more screwed up than in part 1. Some people thought they had a damaged copy because of this sudden ending.<br />And the story itself was not only cliché it was all so jumbled together that it was hard to say whether something was historically inaccurate or one of the many plotholes.<br />And I just didn't understand what they were doing. They already messed up the character in part 1 and it was no better here. And why are they doing this? This is not fair to the fans whom they make hate this version of Magnus.<br /><br />PS. In this story he is the same character he would be more than 200 years later: when there is real trouble he runs away.<br />Full review: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/622515558">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a><br /><br /><u>
  <b>Part 3</b>
</u><br />From here on forward it went downhill. The other parts at least caused an emotional reaction within me; this barely did. Often I asked myself: What is this crap?<br />Any character complexity is just an illusion and a sign of the authors' bad writing. The new characters are not even new. Apparently they cannot think of anything new, smart or realistic.<br />In addition there was a certain "typo" fixed here but in the first e-books where I can only say: that is laziness! The fact that this obvious error actually came into a published e-book is very telling of how little the makers actually care.<br />And don't get me started on the screwed up history both inside and outside the book universe and the badly represented Victorian London, done as bad as in TID.<br />Full review: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/642847797">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a><br /><br />PS. This story has the first claim that Magnus is not into blonds, trust me, the following stories will not reflect that.<br /><br /><u>
  <b>Part 4</b>
</u><br />This was so bad, the first sentence made my eyes role.<br />Once again the authors tried to make Magnus look mature, sympathetic and intelligent, but end up showing an idiot whom you are better not friends with since he is a hypocritical asshole. Who has friends like this doesn't need enemies.<br />And their writing was as if they were pushing buttons to make us feel this and that and all the while what they write contradicts those buttons.<br />This was the first part that read as though these authors only throw raw ideas on paper and call that good storytelling. And that made me doubt whether they actually tried to produce something good.<br />Full review: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/668344904">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a><br /><br /><br /><u>
  <b>Part 5</b>
</u><br />Basically this was boring, slow, full of clichés, continued bad patterns, was lazily written, full of plotholes, had a dumb story and a dumb main character, the villains are a joke and the climax totally anticlimactic.<br />If there is a theme here it is in my eyes "better in comparison". And even this "better" is only in regard to the fact that the switching from Brennan to Johnson as co-author has led to a significant decrease in the number of weird and crazy phrases so typical for Clare's books. But apart from that there is no improvement whatsoever, especially in terms of historical accuracy.<br /><br />PS. When you talk about Black Harlem in the 1920s and then only mention music as a positive thing about it that could be perceived as racist, especially since the book plays at the time of the Harlem Renaissance.<br />Full review: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/682314614">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a><br /><br /><u>
  <b>Part 6</b>
</u><br />This contradicts itself and all the other books of the same universe. All attempts there were of saving Magnus were ruined; and in my eyes it was too late anyway.<br />I will give it credit for trying to make Magnus look mature and Raphael a 3-dimensional character, but it was torpedoed by making Raphael more like an emo Gary Stu and Magnus act like an idiot. Of course every opportunity of Magnus whining was used as it seems. The story seemed to try to make both look smart by having all others act so stupid I sometimes wondered whether they had brain damage.<br />Full review: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/686307964">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a><br /><br /><u>
  <b>Part 7</b>
</u><br />The characters make no sense, the plotholes/conveniences are over the top, the story is predictable and lacks any passion and suspense, it even tries to put an anti-drug message into it (plus some lip service towards gender equality and gay rights), when it's clear that no one there knew what they were talking about, which usually makes the problem that is supposed to be tackled even worse. And don't get me started on what this says about Magnus and his past relationships, especially Camille, or how he reacts towards drugs. This story here made me loose even the tiniest shred of respect that I still had for this asshole.<br />It read like the kind of fan-fiction shippers write who don't care about their characters except for shipping them off with whomever they want and getting the plot into whatever direction they fancy. <br />Actually the biggest plot-convenience of the book (the ending, that also created a lot of plotholes) made me question why this was written in the first place. Because it doesn't make anyone look good and basically opens a giant can of worms.<br />Full review: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/686308654">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a><br /><br /><u>
  <b>Part 8</b>
</u><br />This was basically about Alec and Magnus (between City of Ashes and City of Glass) and it was written without any knowledge toward the subject of closeted gay teens coming from homophobic societies (the way the LGBT topic was handled here was more insulting than anything else in my mind). What is shown of Magnus's and Alec's behavior does not fit what would be going on in such a situation or even how they acted in the other book.<br />In addition: it is obvious that no knowledge as to how to handle supporting characters as more than convenient plot devices was involved or how to let them be in-character and write your world and characters consistently. E.g. Alec is way too confident to be the same guy we see in City of Glass. Also Isabelle doesn't seem to have any problems with her brother dating a criminal.<br /><br />PS. The lip-service for the anti-racism message stinks as usual.<br />Full review: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/686309975">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a><br /><br /><u>
  <b>Part 9</b>
</u><br />These two stories how Magnus meets the Circle in 1989 and later Jocelyn in 1993 were the most useless of the entire franchise. Nothing here makes remotely any sense and from a narrative point of view there is no reason for it to exist in the first place. It answers no open questions, adds nothing and only makes everything worse.<br />The story with the Circle added nothing and made no sense and the story with Jocelyn and Clary was just a retelling of the story we already knew from City of Bones. We already knew how evil Valentine was and after all why would Jocelyn and Luke not tell Clary about it? We have seen Magnus sit on his ass when people are in need, we saw him using his magic in the way only an idiot would, we saw him be a racist and hypocritical asshole. So what was the point of this?<br /><br />PS. I am not going into the topic of the screwed anti-AIDS hysteria message, after all the franchise's screwed pro-LGBT, racial and gender equality and anti-drug messages are already bad enough.<br />Full review: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/686309524">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a><br /><br /><u>
  <b>Part 10</b>
</u><br />I once wrote that the 9th story of the Bane Chronicles was the most useless. This story about the first date of Alec and Magnus is probably the worst. Maybe some others were worse than this, but this one's release date was postponed so often that maybe my memory became hazy.<br />But either way, this story proves in my mind that no one can blame the co-authors that the Bane Chronicles are bad, since this story here is all Cassandra Clare's doing and it has the same and even more flaws than the others.<br />This book didn't even have 30 e-book reader pages of story and it still took me days to finish, there were that many plotholes, weird writing and happenings, barely anything makes sense and every chance that there had been at making this a love and adventure story was torpedoed with a writing incompetence that made the characters look like idiots and/or self-centered jerks.<br />This here is not a story, it is badly written fanfiction of the author herself and the best example on how not to write, anything. Period!<br />Full review: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/686301195">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a><br /><br /><u>
  <b>The bonus story</b>
</u> was just a bunch of messages on Magnus's phone over the course of 3 days. They make Isabelle look like an obsessed fag-hag, let Alec basically grovel, shove one character after another at us (even emo Raphael, Maureen and Maia) and of course want us to sympathize with Magnus. At least Maryse supports her son's decisions.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6917291390297461922" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2843530602" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2658666822395844881">I'm so pleased that Cassandra Clare gave an insight into Magnus' life - how he became, and why he is, the person he is. But seriously, Magnus Bane is actually my fav character in the Shadowhunters series, and my heart broke for him multiple times. That all being said, a few of the stories weren't really my thing, hence the 4 stars. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

+ encodeURIComponent(&#39;cjCvkMNoV/dEAeuzG1e8qHkbbEZYiNyoAgLFBkyIo4ypga/3vP9CIG0vQdBOHqNKPKB6RuFeUyJ19cYJeTNqag==&#39;)}); return false;">next »</a></div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2MmialfDyxVjp5slRG2I01dvoLsUrjvgCceoH9suEWcDeKINKFTewkqJMUYRJJcxEtS2u614tGp+MKsQ7pXYgQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('977eH46TEwE+1pLQOmUYcATnkFd+ed0QXsIQyRDieJUsD9548QQG1hf4OLNvLAeSQVyGV8evUpopNRPGJVmxcw==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer11961434911089865524">Hello Goodreadsers. Here's my official bio:<br/><br/>"Cassandra Clare was born overseas and spent her early years traveling around the world with her family and several trunks of fantasy books.   <span id="freeText11961434911089865524" style="display:none">Hello Goodreadsers. Here's my official bio:<br /><br />"Cassandra Clare was born overseas and spent her early years traveling around the world with her family and several trunks of fantasy books. Cassandra worked for several years as an entertainment journalist for the Hollywood Reporter before turning her attention to fiction. She is the author of City of Bones, the first book in the Mortal Instruments trilogy and a New York Times bestseller. Cassandra lives with her fiance and their two cats in Massachusetts."<br /><br />You can find me online at <br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.cassandraclare.com">www.cassandraclare.com</a><br /><br />I have a blog:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://cassandraclare.livejournal.com/">http://cassandraclare.livejournal.com/</a><br /><br />and a Facebook:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.facebook.com/Cassandraclare">http://www.facebook.com/Cassandraclare</a><br /><br />and a Twitter:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.twitter.com/cassieclare">www.twitter.com/cassieclare</a><br /><br />I'll be available here on Goodreads to answer questions for a Goodreads Author Discussion starting September 18 — <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/37113.Q_A_with_Cassandra_Clare">http://www.goodreads.com/group/show/3...</a><br /><br />Go sign up so you don't miss the conversation when it starts!</span>

            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Where am I?" Magnus croaked.<br />"Nazca."<br />"Oh, so we went on a little trip."<br />"You broke into a man's house," Catarina said. "You stole a carpet and enchanted it to fly. Then you sped off into the night air. We pursued you on foot."<br />"Ah," said Magnus.<br />"You were shouting some things."<br />"What things?"<br />"I prefer not to repeat them," Catarina said. "I also prefer not to remember the time we spent in the desert. It is a mammoth desert, Magnus. Ordinary deserts are quite large. Mammoth deserts are so called because they are larger than ordinary deserts."<br />"Thank you for that interesting and enlightening information," Magnus croaked.<br />"You told us to leave you in the desert, because you planned to start a new life as a cactus," Catarina said, her voice flat. "Then you conjured up tiny needles and threw them at us. With pinpoint accuracy."<br />"Well," he said with dignity. "Considering my highly intoxicated state, you must have been impressed with my aim."<br />"'Impressed' is not the word to use to describe how I felt last night, Magnus."<br />"I thank you for stopping me there," Magnus said. "It was for the best. You are a true friend. No harm done. Let's say no more about it. Could you possibly fetch me - "<br />"Oh, we couldn't stop you," Catarina interrupted. "We tried, but you giggled, leaped onto the carpet, and flew away again. You kept saying that you wanted to go to Moquegua."<br />"What did I do in Moquegua?"<br />"You never got there," Catarina said. "But you were flying about and yelling and trying to, ahem, write messages for us with your carpet in the sky."<br />"We then stopped for a meal," Catarina said. "You were most insistent that we try a local specialty that you called cuy. We actually had a very pleasant meal, even though you were still very drunk."<br />"I'm sure I must have been sobering up at that point," Magnus argued.<br />"Magnus, you were trying to flirt with your own plate."<br />"I'm a very open-minded sort of fellow!"<br />"Ragnor is not," Catarina said. "When he found out that you were feeding us guinea pigs, he hit you over the head with your plate. It broke."<br />"So ended our love," Magnus said. "Ah, well. It would never have worked between me and the plate anyway. I'm sure the food did me good, Catarina, and you were very good to feed me and put me to bed - "<br />Catarina shook her head."You fell down on the floor. Honestly, we thought it best to leave you sleeping on the ground. We thought you would remain there for some time, but we took our eyes off you for one minute, and then you scuttled off. Ragnor claims he saw you making for the carpet, crawling like a huge demented crab.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/1019140-where-am-i-magnus-croaked-nazca-oh-so-we-went">129 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
